The current blue uniform has the serifed word "RANGERS" in red and white drop shadow arranged diagonally, with red and white stripes on the sleeves and tail. Originally, the uniform was light blue, before it switched to a darker classic Rangers "Broadway Blue" in 1929. In addition, the original versions neither had a drop shadow nor were serifed. During the 1946–47 season, the word "RANGERS" was arranged in an arch form above the sweater number. It adopted its current form the next season, along with dropshadowed numbers, except for a brief period where the city name was used, a tie-down collar was not used and the tail and sleeve stripes were separated by thin blue stripes. Red pants have been used with the uniform since the 1929–30 season.<sup>[\[92\]](#cite_note-New_York_Rangers_uniform_history-92)</sup>

The white jerseys were first unveiled in the 1951–52 season, as part of a mandate that regulated NHL teams to have a dark home jersey and a light away jersey. The [serifed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Serif "Serif") word "RANGERS" is also arranged diagonally, but in blue with red drop shadow. A quinticolor of blue, white and red stripes accentuate the tail and sleeves, while a blue shoulder yoke with white and red stripes completes the look. The white sweaters, with minor changes such as a tie-down collar and arched player names, have remained virtually unchanged since.<sup>[\[92\]](#cite_note-New_York_Rangers_uniform_history-92)</sup>

During the tenure of general manager [John Ferguson Sr.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Ferguson_Sr. "John Ferguson Sr."), he sought to modernize the Rangers sweater by featuring rounded numbers, a darker shade of blue and the shield logo, which was unveiled in the 1976–77 season. A blue and red stripe (white and red stripe in the blue sweaters) extend from the yoke to the sleeves, while blue pants were used. However, it proved unpopular with the fans, and following the 1977–78 season it was replaced by an updated version of their classic uniforms. Ferguson used this similar design when he became GM of the original [Winnipeg Jets](<https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Winnipeg_Jets_(1972–1996)> "Winnipeg Jets (1972–1996)").<sup>[\[93\]](#cite_note-93)</sup>

<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:AveryNYR.jpg" class="image"><img src="http://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/AveryNYR.jpg/220px-AveryNYR.jpg" class="thumbimage" srcset="
                      //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/AveryNYR.jpg/330px-AveryNYR.jpg 1.5x,
                      //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/ae/AveryNYR.jpg                          2x
                    " width="220" height="186" /></a>

<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:AveryNYR.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>

From 1996 to 2007 the Rangers' alternate jersey featured the head of the Statue of Liberty with the team abbreviation below it.

The modernized classic uniforms introduced in 1978 featured some subtle changes. Both jerseys featured a V-neck collar in a red-white-red pattern, and bolder stripes on the sleeves and waistline. On the blue jersey, the red and white stripes were separated by thin blue stripes, along with the waistline stripes being raised above the hemline so that the patterns on both jerseys matched. From 1978 to 1987, the blue jersey (then the road jersey) featured "NEW YORK" diagonally across the front instead of the traditional "RANGERS" wordmark, similar to their current heritage alternate jerseys.<sup>[\[94\]](#cite_note-94)</sup> In 1997, the Rangers reverted the blue jersey's design, restoring the old striping pattern, and becoming the first team to re-introduce lace-up collars.<sup>[\[95\]](#cite_note-95)</sup> The white jerseys followed suit in 1999,<sup>[\[96\]](#cite_note-96)</sup> and the design was carried over to the Reebok Edge template in 2007.<sup>[\[97\]](#cite_note-97)</sup>

The Rangers previously had a navy alternate jersey featuring the head of the [Statue of Liberty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Statue_of_Liberty "Statue of Liberty") with the team abbreviation (NYR) below in a futuristic script. Silver was used as an accent color, but the player names and numbers retain the same color schemes as the regular jerseys, except for a darker shade of blue. Other than a white version used in the 1998–99 season, this jersey was used from 1996 to 2007, and proved to be highly popular with fans.<sup>[\[98\]](#cite_note-98)</sup>

During the 2010–11 season, the Rangers debuted a heritage blue jersey as their new alternate uniform. The jersey features a darker shade a blue, as well as a cream trim. Unlike the regular jerseys, the font of the alternate is in [sans-serif](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sans-serif "Sans-serif") and does not feature a dropshadow, much like the original Rangers jersey. The Rangers wore the jerseys at home on Saturdays and when they played against Original Six teams.<sup>[\[92\]](#cite_note-New_York_Rangers_uniform_history-92)</sup> For the 2017–18 season, the heritage jersey was retired because of the league-wide switch to the [Adidas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adidas "Adidas") uniform format.

In the [2012 NHL Winter Classic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_NHL_Winter_Classic "2012 NHL Winter Classic"), the Rangers wore a cream jersey combining classic and current styles. A different version of the shield logo was used, while the player names were arranged in a straight line. The stripes were also lessened, giving it a minimalist, vintage look, as most Winter Classic jerseys are.<sup>[\[99\]](#cite_note-99)</sup>

For the [2014 NHL Stadium Series](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2014_NHL_Stadium_Series "2014 NHL Stadium Series"), the Rangers used white jerseys with the city name in navy, silver and red. In addition, they feature diagonal stripes and sleeve numbers, and enlarged numbers on the back to make them more readable to spectators. The chrome version of the shield logo is placed in the left shoulder. Like the Winter Classic sweaters, player names are in a straight position.<sup>[\[100\]](#cite_note-100)</sup>

The [2018 NHL Winter Classic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2018_NHL_Winter_Classic "2018 NHL Winter Classic") saw the Rangers wear a navy jersey with a combination of elements from prior uniform designs. The striping design was inspired from their current uniforms, while the white "RANGERS" wordmark was a nod from the team's late 1920s jerseys. A white silhouette of the Rangers' shield logo contained either the abbreviation "N.Y." or the alternate captain "A" and captain "C" designations. Player names are arranged in a straight position.<sup>[\[101\]](#cite_note-101)</sup>

During the 2020–21 season, the Rangers released a "Reverse Retro" alternate uniform in collaboration with Adidas. The uniform featured the "Lady Liberty" design worn from 1996 to 2007, but with a few changes in the striping.<sup>[\[102\]](#cite_note-102)</sup>

## <span id="Season-by-season_record" class="mw-headline">Season-by-season record</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\[</span>[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=New_York_Rangers&action=edit&section=11 "Edit section: Season-by-season record")<span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\]</span></span>

### <span id="Team_captains" class="mw-headline">Team captains</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\[</span>[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=New_York_Rangers&action=edit&section=14 "Edit section: Team captains")<span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\]</span></span>

<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Brian_Leetch_New_York_Rangers_1997_Vancouver.jpg" class="image"><img src="http://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Brian_Leetch_New_York_Rangers_1997_Vancouver.jpg/170px-Brian_Leetch_New_York_Rangers_1997_Vancouver.jpg" class="thumbimage" srcset="
                      //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Brian_Leetch_New_York_Rangers_1997_Vancouver.jpg/255px-Brian_Leetch_New_York_Rangers_1997_Vancouver.jpg 1.5x,
                      //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Brian_Leetch_New_York_Rangers_1997_Vancouver.jpg/340px-Brian_Leetch_New_York_Rangers_1997_Vancouver.jpg 2x
                    " width="170" height="240" /></a>

<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Brian_Leetch_New_York_Rangers_1997_Vancouver.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>

[Brian Leetch](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brian_Leetch "Brian Leetch") was the 23rd captain in Rangers history, maintaining the position from 1997 to 2000.

- [Bill Cook](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bill_Cook "Bill Cook"), 1926–1937
- [Art Coulter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Art_Coulter "Art Coulter"), 1937–1942
- [Ott Heller](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ehrhardt_Heller "Ehrhardt Heller"), 1942–1945
- [Neil Colville](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neil_Colville "Neil Colville"), 1945–1948
- [Buddy O'Connor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Buddy_O%27Connor "Buddy O'Connor"), 1949–1950
- [Frank Eddolls](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frank_Eddolls "Frank Eddolls"), 1950–1951
- [Allan Stanley](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allan_Stanley "Allan Stanley"), 1951–1953
- [Don Raleigh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Don_Raleigh "Don Raleigh"), 1953–1955
- [Harry Howell](<https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harry_Howell_(ice_hockey)> "Harry Howell (ice hockey)"), 1955–1957
- <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_Sullivan_(ice_hockey)" class="mw-redirect" title="George Sullivan (ice hockey)">George Sullivan</a>, 1957–1961
- [Andy Bathgate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Andy_Bathgate "Andy Bathgate"), 1961–1964
- [Camille Henry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Camille_Henry "Camille Henry"), 1964–1965
- [Bob Nevin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bob_Nevin "Bob Nevin"), 1965–1971
- [Vic Hadfield](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vic_Hadfield "Vic Hadfield"), 1971–1974
- [Brad Park](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brad_Park "Brad Park"), 1974–1975
- [Phil Esposito](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phil_Esposito "Phil Esposito"), 1975–1978
- [Dave Maloney](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dave_Maloney "Dave Maloney"), 1978–1980
- [Walt Tkaczuk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Walt_Tkaczuk "Walt Tkaczuk"), 1980–1981
- [Barry Beck](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Barry_Beck "Barry Beck"), 1981–1986
- [Ron Greschner](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ron_Greschner "Ron Greschner"), 1986–1987
- [Kelly Kisio](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kelly_Kisio "Kelly Kisio"), 1987–1991
- [Mark Messier](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mark_Messier "Mark Messier"), 1991–1997
- [Brian Leetch](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brian_Leetch "Brian Leetch"), 1997–2000
- Mark Messier, 2000–2004<sup>[\[105\]](#cite_note-105)</sup>
- [Jaromir Jagr](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jaromír_Jágr "Jaromír Jágr"), 2006–2008
- [Chris Drury](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chris_Drury "Chris Drury"), 2008–2011
- [Ryan Callahan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ryan_Callahan "Ryan Callahan"), 2011–2014
- [Ryan McDonagh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ryan_McDonagh "Ryan McDonagh"), 2014–2018

### <span id="General_managers" class="mw-headline">General managers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\[</span>[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=New_York_Rangers&action=edit&section=15 "Edit section: General managers")<span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\]</span></span>

Further information: [List of New York Rangers general managers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_New_York_Rangers_general_managers "List of New York Rangers general managers")

The current general manager is [Chris Drury](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chris_Drury "Chris Drury"), who had been named on May 5, 2021.<sup>[\[106\]](#cite_note-106)</sup>

### <span id="Head_coaches" class="mw-headline">Head coaches</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\[</span>[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=New_York_Rangers&action=edit&section=16 "Edit section: Head coaches")<span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\]</span></span>

Further information: [List of New York Rangers head coaches](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_New_York_Rangers_head_coaches "List of New York Rangers head coaches")

The current head coach is [Gerard Gallant](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gerard_Gallant "Gerard Gallant"), who has served since June 16, 2021.<sup>[\[91\]](#cite_note-Gallant0616-91)</sup>

## <span id="Team_and_league_honors" class="mw-headline">Team and league honors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\[</span>[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=New_York_Rangers&action=edit&section=17 "Edit section: Team and league honors")<span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\]</span></span>

### <span id="Awards_and_trophies" class="mw-headline">Awards and trophies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\[</span>[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=New_York_Rangers&action=edit&section=18 "Edit section: Awards and trophies")<span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\]</span></span>

Main article: [List of New York Rangers award winners](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_New_York_Rangers_award_winners "List of New York Rangers award winners")

The following lists the league awards which have been won by the Rangers team and its players and alumni:<sup>\[_[<span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2011)">citation\ needed</span>](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")_\]</sup>

**[Stanley Cup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stanley_Cup "Stanley Cup")**

- [1927–28](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1927–28_NHL_season "1927–28 NHL season"), [1932–33](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1932–33_NHL_season "1932–33 NHL season"), [1939–40](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1939–40_NHL_season "1939–40 NHL season"), [1993–94](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1993–94_NHL_season "1993–94 NHL season")

**[Victoria Cup](<https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Victoria_Cup_(ice_hockey)> "Victoria Cup (ice hockey)")**

- [2008 Victoria Cup](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2008_Victoria_Cup "2008 Victoria Cup")

**[Presidents' Trophy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Presidents%27_Trophy "Presidents' Trophy")**

- [1991–92](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1991–92_NHL_season "1991–92 NHL season"), [1993–94](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1993–94_NHL_season "1993–94 NHL season"), [2014–15](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2014–15_NHL_season "2014–15 NHL season")

**[Prince of Wales Trophy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prince_of_Wales_Trophy "Prince of Wales Trophy")**

- [1931–32](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1931–32_NHL_season "1931–32 NHL season"), [1941–42](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1941–42_NHL_season "1941–42 NHL season"), [1993–94](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1993–94_NHL_season "1993–94 NHL season"), [2013–14](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2013–14_NHL_season "2013–14 NHL season")

**[O'Brien Cup](<https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/O%27Brien_Trophy_(ice_hockey)> "O'Brien Trophy (ice hockey)")**

- [1949–50](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1949–50_NHL_season "1949–50 NHL season")

**[Bill Masterton Memorial Trophy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bill_Masterton_Memorial_Trophy "Bill Masterton Memorial Trophy")**

- [Jean Ratelle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jean_Ratelle "Jean Ratelle"): [1970–71](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1970–71_NHL_season "1970–71 NHL season")
- [Rod Gilbert](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rod_Gilbert "Rod Gilbert"): [1975–76](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1975–76_NHL_season "1975–76 NHL season")
- [Anders Hedberg](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anders_Hedberg "Anders Hedberg"): [1984–85](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1984–85_NHL_season "1984–85 NHL season")
- [Adam Graves](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adam_Graves "Adam Graves"): [2000–01](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2000–01_NHL_season "2000–01 NHL season")
- [Dominic Moore](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dominic_Moore "Dominic Moore"): [2013–14](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2013–14_NHL_season "2013–14 NHL season")

**[Calder Memorial Trophy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Calder_Memorial_Trophy "Calder Memorial Trophy")**

- [Kilby MacDonald](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kilby_MacDonald "Kilby MacDonald"): [1939–40](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1939–40_NHL_season "1939–40 NHL season")
- [Grant Warwick](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grant_Warwick "Grant Warwick"): [1941–42](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1941–42_NHL_season "1941–42 NHL season")
- [Edgar Laprade](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Edgar_Laprade "Edgar Laprade"): [1945–46](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1945–46_NHL_season "1945–46 NHL season")
- [Pentti Lund](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pentti_Lund "Pentti Lund"): [1948–49](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1948–49_NHL_season "1948–49 NHL season")
- [Gump Worsley](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gump_Worsley "Gump Worsley"): [1952–53](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1952–53_NHL_season "1952–53 NHL season")
- [Camille Henry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Camille_Henry "Camille Henry"): [1953–54](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1953–54_NHL_season "1953–54 NHL season")
- [Steve Vickers](<https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Steve_Vickers_(ice_hockey)> "Steve Vickers (ice hockey)"): [1972–73](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1972–73_NHL_season "1972–73 NHL season")
- [Brian Leetch](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brian_Leetch "Brian Leetch"): [1988–89](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1988–89_NHL_season "1988–89 NHL season")

**[Conn Smythe Trophy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conn_Smythe_Trophy "Conn Smythe Trophy")**

- [Brian Leetch](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brian_Leetch "Brian Leetch"): [1993–94](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1993–94_NHL_season "1993–94 NHL season")

**[Hart Memorial Trophy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hart_Memorial_Trophy "Hart Memorial Trophy")**

- [Buddy O'Connor](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Buddy_O%27Connor "Buddy O'Connor"): [1947–48](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1947–48_NHL_season "1947–48 NHL season")
- [Chuck Rayner](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chuck_Rayner "Chuck Rayner"): [1949–50](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1949–50_NHL_season "1949–50 NHL season")
- [Andy Bathgate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Andy_Bathgate "Andy Bathgate"): [1958–59](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1958–59_NHL_season "1958–59 NHL season")

### <span id="Hall_of_Famers" class="mw-headline">Hall of Famers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\[</span>[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=New_York_Rangers&action=edit&section=20 "Edit section: Hall of Famers")<span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\]</span></span>

The New York Rangers acknowledge an affiliation with a number of inductees to the [Hockey Hall of Fame](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hockey_Hall_of_Fame "Hockey Hall of Fame"). Rangers inductees include 53 former players and nine builders of the sport.<sup>[\[116\]](#cite_note-medgu-116)</sup> The nine individuals recognized as builders by the Hall of Fame includes former Rangers executives, general managers, head coaches, and owners. In addition to players and builders, several broadcasters were also awarded the [Foster Hewitt Memorial Award](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Foster_Hewitt_Memorial_Award "Foster Hewitt Memorial Award") from the Hockey Hall of Fame. [Sal Messina](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sal_Messina "Sal Messina"), a [color commentator](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Color_commentator "Color commentator"), was the first Rangers broadcaster to be awarded the Foster Hewitt Memorial Award. Other Rangers broadcasters awarded the Foster Hewitt Memorial Award include [John Davidson](<https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Davidson_(ice_hockey)> "John Davidson (ice hockey)") (awarded in 2009), and [Sam Rosen](<https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sam_Rosen_(sportscaster)> "Sam Rosen (sportscaster)") (awarded in 2016).<sup>[\[117\]](#cite_note-117)</sup>

### <span id="Retired_numbers" class="mw-headline">Retired numbers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\[</span>[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=New_York_Rangers&action=edit&section=21 "Edit section: Retired numbers")<span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\]</span></span>

<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:NY_Rangers_Banner_2_35.jpg" class="image"><img src="http://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/NY_Rangers_Banner_2_35.jpg/220px-NY_Rangers_Banner_2_35.jpg" class="thumbimage" srcset="
                      //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/NY_Rangers_Banner_2_35.jpg/330px-NY_Rangers_Banner_2_35.jpg 1.5x,
                      //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/NY_Rangers_Banner_2_35.jpg/440px-NY_Rangers_Banner_2_35.jpg 2x
                    " width="220" height="214" /></a>

<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:NY_Rangers_Banner_2_35.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>

Retired numbers hang from the rafters of [Madison Square Garden](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Madison_Square_Garden "Madison Square Garden").

The Rangers have retired eight numbers for ten players in their history, and the NHL retired [Wayne Gretzky](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wayne_Gretzky "Wayne Gretzky")'s No. 99 for all its member teams at the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/50th_National_Hockey_League_All-Star_Game" class="mw-redirect" title="50th National Hockey League All-Star Game">2000 NHL All-Star Game</a>.<sup>[\[118\]](#cite_note-118)</sup>

### <span id="Single-season_records" class="mw-headline">Single-season records</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\[</span>[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=New_York_Rangers&action=edit&section=22 "Edit section: Single-season records")<span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\]</span></span>

Main article: [List of New York Rangers records](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_New_York_Rangers_records "List of New York Rangers records")

- Points: **[Jaromir Jagr](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jaromír_Jágr "Jaromír Jágr")** (2005–06) – 123<sup>[\[127\]](#cite_note-records-127)</sup>
- Goals: **[Jaromir Jagr](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jaromír_Jágr "Jaromír Jágr")** (2005–06) – 54<sup>[\[127\]](#cite_note-records-127)</sup>
- Assists: **[Brian Leetch](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brian_Leetch "Brian Leetch")** (1991–92) – 80<sup>[\[127\]](#cite_note-records-127)</sup>
- Power play goals: **[Jaromir Jagr](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jaromír_Jágr "Jaromír Jágr")** (2005–06) – 24<sup>[\[127\]](#cite_note-records-127)</sup>
- Power play points: **[Brian Leetch](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brian_Leetch "Brian Leetch")** (1993–94) – 53<sup>[\[127\]](#cite_note-records-127)</sup>
- Power play assists: **[Brian Leetch](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brian_Leetch "Brian Leetch")** (1990–91) – 45<sup>[\[128\]](#cite_note-records_2-128)</sup>
- Short-handed goals: **[Theoren Fleury](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theoren_Fleury "Theoren Fleury")** (2000–01) – 7<sup>[\[127\]](#cite_note-records-127)</sup>
- Short-handed points: **[Mark Messier](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mark_Messier "Mark Messier")** (1996–97) – 11<sup>[\[127\]](#cite_note-records-127)</sup>
- Short-handed assists: **[Mark Messier](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mark_Messier "Mark Messier")** (1993–94) – 7<sup>[\[128\]](#cite_note-records_2-128)</sup>

- Even strength goals: **[Jean Ratelle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jean_Ratelle "Jean Ratelle")** (1971–72) – 40<sup>[\[129\]](#cite_note-records_3-129)</sup>
- Even strength points: **[Jean Ratelle](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jean_Ratelle "Jean Ratelle")** (1971–72) – 82<sup>[\[128\]](#cite_note-records_2-128)</sup>
- Even strength assists: **[Mark Messier](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mark_Messier "Mark Messier")** (1991–92), **[Wayne Gretzky](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wayne_Gretzky "Wayne Gretzky")** (1996–97), & **[Artemi Panarin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artemi_Panarin "Artemi Panarin")** (2019–20) – 46<sup>[\[128\]](#cite_note-records_2-128)</sup>
- Game-winning goals: **6 players** <sup>[\[a\]](#cite_note-fn2-130)</sup> — 9
- Overtime goals: **[Tomas Sandstrom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tomas_Sandström "Tomas Sandström")** (1986–87), **[Adam Graves](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adam_Graves "Adam Graves")** (1998–99), & **[Marian Gaborik](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marián_Gáborík "Marián Gáborík")** (2011–12) – 3<sup>[\[127\]](#cite_note-records-127)</sup>
- Empty net goals: **[Michael Grabner](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michael_Grabner "Michael Grabner")** (2017–18) – 7<sup>[\[129\]](#cite_note-records_3-129)</sup>

- Plus/minus: **[Brad Park](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brad_Park "Brad Park")** (1971–72) – +63 / **[Ron Greschner](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ron_Greschner "Ron Greschner")** (1975–76) – -50<sup>[\[127\]](#cite_note-records-127)</sup>
- Shots on goal: **[Jaromir Jagr](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jaromír_Jágr "Jaromír Jágr")** (2005–06) – 368<sup>[\[127\]](#cite_note-records-127)</sup>
- Penalty minutes: **[Troy Mallette](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Troy_Mallette "Troy Mallette")** (1989–90) – 305<sup>[\[127\]](#cite_note-records-127)</sup>
- Goaltending wins: **[Mike Richter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mike_Richter "Mike Richter")** (1993–94) – 42<sup>[\[130\]](#cite_note-records_goalie-131)</sup>
- Goaltending shutouts: **[John Ross Roach](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Ross_Roach "John Ross Roach")** (1928–1929) – 13<sup>[\[130\]](#cite_note-records_goalie-131)</sup>
- Goaltending saves: **[Gump Worsley](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gump_Worsley "Gump Worsley")** (1955–1956) – 2376<sup>[\[130\]](#cite_note-records_goalie-131)</sup>

All single-season records verifiable from: <a href="http://www.nhl.com/" class="external text">Official Site of the National Hockey League | NHL.com</a>

### <span id="Franchise_scoring_leaders" class="mw-headline">Franchise scoring leaders</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\[</span>[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=New_York_Rangers&action=edit&section=23 "Edit section: Franchise scoring leaders")<span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\]</span></span>

These are the top-ten-point-scorers in franchise history. Figures are updated after each completed NHL regular season.<sup>[\[131\]](#cite_note-132)</sup>

<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Walt_Tkaczuk_80-81.JPG" class="image"><img src="http://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Walt_Tkaczuk_80-81.JPG/170px-Walt_Tkaczuk_80-81.JPG" class="thumbimage" srcset="
                      //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Walt_Tkaczuk_80-81.JPG/255px-Walt_Tkaczuk_80-81.JPG 1.5x,
                      //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Walt_Tkaczuk_80-81.JPG/340px-Walt_Tkaczuk_80-81.JPG 2x
                    " width="170" height="225" /></a>

<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Walt_Tkaczuk_80-81.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>

Playing with the Rangers from 1968 to 1981, [Walt Tkaczuk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Walt_Tkaczuk "Walt Tkaczuk") scored the sixth most points in the franchise (678 points).

- <span class="legend-color" style="
                      background-color: #ccffcc;
                      color: black;
                      border: 1px solid darkgray;
                    "> \* </span> – current Rangers player

6.  <span id="cite_note-6"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">**[^](#cite_ref-6)**</span> <span class="reference-text">Boucher, Frank; Frayne, Trent (1973). _When the Rangers Were Young_. New York: Dodd, Mead & Company. p. 74. <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> [0-396-06852-9](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special:BookSources/0-396-06852-9 "Special:BookSources/0-396-06852-9"). <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/LCCN_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="LCCN (identifier)">LCCN</a> <a href="http://lccn.loc.gov/73007485" class="external text">73007485</a>. <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OCLC_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="OCLC (identifier)">OCLC</a> <a href="http://www.worldcat.org/oclc/799524" class="external text">799524</a>. <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/OL_(identifier)" class="mw-redirect" title="OL (identifier)">OL</a> <a href="http://openlibrary.org/books/OL5415647M" class="external text">5415647M</a>. “Even before our training camp opened we were widely known as Tex's Rangers, a name given us by George Daley, the sports editor of the New York _Herald Tribune_, and one that seemed likely to stick. In fact, our first team crest was that of a horse sketched in blue carrying a cowboy waving a hockey stick aloft. The horse was rearing, with the word TEX'S in a crescent at the top of the emblem with RANGERS looped below. But Rickard didn't like the idea and before the season opened our insignia was changed to the present diagonal splash of the word RANGERS.”<span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=When+the+Rangers+Were+Young&amp;rft.place=New+York&amp;rft.pages=74&amp;rft.pub=Dodd%2C+Mead+%26+Company&amp;rft.date=1973&amp;rft_id=info%3Aoclcnum%2F799524&amp;rft_id=info%3Alccn%2F73007485&amp;rft_id=%2F%2Fopenlibrary.org%2Fbooks%2FOL5415647M%23id-name%3DOL&amp;rft.isbn=0-396-06852-9&amp;rft.aulast=Boucher&amp;rft.aufirst=Frank&amp;rft.au=Frayne%2C+Trent&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ANew+York+Rangers"></span></span></span>
